Yang Case: A Special Tribunal Will Be Formed to Try the Murderer; Yang's Body Has Been Placed in a Coffin and Will Be Moved to Wuchang; A Funeral Committee Has Been Established, Headed by He Chengjun; Meng Guangpeng Serves as Acting Provincial Chairman 72

Hankou Correspondence: After the assassination of Provincial Chairman Yang Yongtai in Hankou, his body was moved to the Bankers' Association. The entire Provincial Government Committee held an emergency meeting that evening and appointed Lu Zhu, a member of the Provincial Committee and Secretary-General, as acting chairman and reported it to the Central Government for record. On the 26th, a public notice was issued to all sectors, and the Provincial Government and all departments continued to operate as usual. However, the regular meeting on that day was suspended to express mourning. Yang's body was originally scheduled to be placed in a coffin on the 26th, but it was postponed by one day because his eldest daughter, Ms. Yixi, had not yet arrived. Many people from all walks of life went to the mourning hall to pay their respects. A telegram of condolence from the Central Executive Committee has also arrived in Hubei. Military and political dignitaries and consuls from various countries in Hankou have also sent telegrams of condolence, totaling more than a thousand. The funeral preparatory office held a meeting at the Bankers' Association on the 26th and resolved nine points: (1) A small coffin will be placed at 3:00 AM on the 27th. After Chairman Yang's family arrives, a large coffin will be placed; (2) The coffin will be moved to the newly built library in Baobingtang, Wuchang, on a scheduled date; (3) The funeral committee will move to the Provincial Government office after the coffin is moved to Wuchang; (4) The memorial service will be held in the Provincial Government; (5) On the day of the coffin's movement and the memorial service, all of Hubei Province will fly flags at half-mast to express mourning; (6) The funeral committee will be officially established on the same day, and the name of the preparatory office will be abolished; (7) He Chengjun is appointed as the director of the funeral committee, and Chen Jicheng and Lu Zhu are appointed as deputy directors; (8) A ceremony group will be added to the funeral committee, and Li Shucheng will be appointed as the chief clerk; (9) Chen Fang is appointed as the chief clerk of the document group, Deng Xiangyu and Yu Huanzheng are appointed as deputy chief clerks, Cheng Qibao is appointed as the chief clerk of the reception group, Jia Shiyi is appointed as the chief clerk of the accounting group, Nan Kui and Zhou Qian are appointed as deputy chief clerks, Meng Guangpeng is appointed as the chief clerk of the general affairs group, Xing Yaoshen, Jia Baosan, and Cheng Wenxun are appointed as deputy chief clerks, Liu Shoupeng is appointed as the chief clerk of the arrangement group, He Hengfu, Jin Jutang, and Hong Yanbin are appointed as deputy chief clerks, Liu Zushun is appointed as the chief clerk of the security group, Cai Mengjian and Wang Yufen are appointed as deputy chief clerks, Li Shucheng is appointed as the chief clerk of the ceremony group, and Yi Jueqian and Ye Jialong are appointed as deputy chief clerks. The decision was immediately announced to all parties to start work. The incident was very sudden. According to eyewitnesses, at about 1:00 PM on the 25th, a person was wandering on a wharf along the riverbank, sitting on a bench on the sidewalk. When he saw a car arrive, he immediately stood up. It was said that he had been waiting for Yang for two hours. At 3:15 PM, Yang's car arrived at a wharf. After getting out of the car and stepping onto the stone steps, the murderer rushed forward, pulled out a gun, and shot. After Yang was shot, his guards chased after the murderer and fired six shots, but missed. The ammunition was exhausted. The murderer dropped his pistol while fleeing. He turned back to pick it up, but the police on duty arrived and stopped him. The police in front came out to intercept him and finally captured him. The crowd beat him up, but the murderer remained calm and stopped them from beating him, saying, "I am not an ignorant person. I can go with you." Later, after strict interrogation, he confessed his name as Cheng Xiechao and admitted to assassinating Yang, claiming that he had been in Hankou for a long time and had lived in the Taian Inn on He Street. He moved to the Jinghan Hotel on the 18th. The military and political authorities decided that the case would be tried by a special military court jointly formed by the Pacification Headquarters, the Garrison Command, the Provincial Government, the Municipal Government, the Public Security Bureau, and the Gendarmerie Corps. It is believed that some clues can be obtained from this. As for the five suspects arrested at the Jinghan Hotel, they were jointly tried by the Investigation Division and the Gendarmerie Corps at the police station on the 26th. After investigation, it was confirmed that they were not related to the case, and they were all released on bail. (October 26th)

Hankou Correspondence: Provincial Chairman Yang Yongtai was assassinated in front of the Jianghan Customs House in Hankou the other day. This is the first time since 1926 that a high-ranking official has been killed by thugs. Chairman Lin of the National Government and President Jiang of the Executive Yuan have sent telegrams of condolence to his family. Central Party, government, and military institutions have also sent Liu Bohua, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government, to Hubei to offer condolences. Liu arrived in Hankou by plane from Nanjing at 12:00 noon on the 27th and arrived at 2:40 PM. Yang's eldest daughter, Ms. Yixi, third daughter, Ms. Qiuxi, fourth daughter, Ms. Yanxi, and fifth daughter, Ms. Chenxi, also arrived by China Aviation Corporation plane from Shanghai. At that time, Yang's body had already been placed in a small coffin at 3:00 AM. They wept bitterly over the coffin, and the scene was extremely tragic. However, his wife, Ms. Li Wuzhen, remained in Shanghai due to illness. His second daughter is studying in England, and although a telegram has been sent to notify her, it is feared that she will not be able to return to China. His sixth daughter, Ms. Xi, and son, Huaixi, were with Yang in Hubei. The funeral committee, considering that Yang's family had arrived, placed Yang's body in a large coffin at 6:00 PM and held a public memorial service, presided over by Liu Zhenhua, He Chengjun, and Lu Zhu.

Liu Zhenhua, the Central Government Representative, wrote in his eulogy: "On this 28th day of October in the 25th year of the Republic of China, the day of the great coffin placement of the late Chairman Yang Changqing of the Hubei Provincial Government, Zhenhua, on behalf of the Central Government, came by plane to offer sacrifices with wine, flowers, and incense to the spirit of my brother Changqing. Zhenhua was in Nanjing when he suddenly heard the news of the misfortune. My heart was broken, and I could not eat or sleep in peace. Therefore, despite my weak health, I chartered a plane to Hubei, wanting to see my old friend one last time before the coffin was closed. Now, his face is still the same, but his voice and appearance are gone. Where should these tears of grief come from? Zhenhua's grief is not the private grief of one person. It is because my brother's body was a pillar of the country, an arm of Chairman Jiang. Now that my brother is dead, the country has lost a pillar, and Chairman Jiang has lost an arm. How can the loss be measured? Therefore, today's crying is not Zhenhua's crying for his brother, but the crying of all those who are heartbroken throughout the country. I still remember our casual conversations, and my brother often said with emotion that we should follow Chairman Jiang's efforts to rebuild the country and the nation, so that we can also be virtuous assistants of the Zhongxing. How could I have thought that my brother would not fulfill his ambition, would not see the Zhongxing of the country, and would leave us to die first? However, my brother's ambition is also our ambition. From now on, we can only follow Chairman Jiang and redouble our efforts to complete the cause of national revival to comfort my brother's spirit in heaven. What is most unbearable is that my brother died suddenly with a heart full of patriotic enthusiasm, and without leaving a single word of his will. With my brother's noble character, like the Chengdu mulberry and the Hunan orange, combined with a weak wife and young children, he left without looking back. This is truly something that makes my heart break every time I think about it. However, the unfinished business of my brother today is the responsibility of those who survive him. Moreover, my brother is very smart and will surely have achievements in the future, and will be able to continue my brother's legacy. Let my brother be comforted in the afterlife. This is something that can be foreseen by heaven and humanity. It is so sad, so painful, Chang brother, Chang brother, do you know my sorrow? Enjoy the sacrifice."

He Chengjun and representatives of Party, government, military, police, and other organizations wrote in their eulogy: "On this 27th day of October in the 25th year of the Republic of China, He Chengjun, Special Envoy of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang stationed in Hubei and Pacification Director, led representatives of Party, government, military, police, and other organizations to offer sacrifices to the spirit of the late Chairman Yang of the Hubei Provincial Government, saying, 'Looking back at our public, containing plans and expressing loyalty, presiding over the Altar, discussing with breadth and depth, controlling financial power, taking on heavy responsibilities, achieving merit in our hometown, and being respected in Guangzhou. When assisting Yuanrong, serving in three provinces, planning in the tent, deciding victories and predicting enemies, We were bestowed with trust and appointed to the border region, rejuvenating Jianghan, praising the customs of Jianghan, Zhou official six lines, Guanzi four dimensions, clarifying the essentials, advocating grand rules. Given time, we hoped for great governance. How could we have imagined that we would be ambushed and that the virtuous would suddenly pass away? The shocking news spread, and we shared the same boat through storms, sharing worries and dangers. Since we have entrusted our sincere friendship, we feel even more grief. White horses and plain cars mourn at the mourning hall, pouring wine into the cup, and offering sumptuous dishes. May the gods come and be on our side. Alas, enjoy the sacrifice.'"

The Hubei Provincial Government wrote in its eulogy: "On this 27th day of October in the 25th year of the Republic of China, Lu Zhu and other members of the Hubei Provincial Government and officials of all subordinate agencies respectfully offer sacrifices to the spirit of the late Chairman Yang, saying, 'Oh, our public, with extraordinary talent, early participation in the National Assembly, upright words and eloquence, opening the mansion in Guangdong, grand facilities, assisting Yuanrong, meritorious deeds in the tent, going out to suppress Hubei, nourishing Jianghan, bearing heavy burdens and reaching far, adhering to the three lines, working diligently day and night, governing and planning, and all measures were taken. It has already taken shape, Yiyang Zhibiao, Nampithe similar, recorded in the history books, demonstrating political transformation. Alas, my colleagues, fortunately relying on leadership, inspiring our spirit, and hoping for great achievements. Unfortunately, Wu Tian did not pity us, and we were suddenly ambushed. With a single gaze of composure, alas, our Uncle, the Nanguo Gan Tang, always cherishes the fear of Zhao, the Chu xie soars, and the Jiuquan does not work, alas, enjoy the sacrifice."

Yang's coffin has now been decided by the funeral committee to be moved to the newly built Provincial Library in Baobingtang, Wuchang, on the 2nd of next month, and a memorial service will be held at a later date. After Yang's death, the entire Provincial Government Committee, in order to ensure that government affairs are not interrupted, appointed Lu Zhu, a member of the committee and Secretary-General, to temporarily act as chairman and take temporary responsibility. At the same time, they telegraphed President Jiang to send someone to preside over the matter. It is reported that Jiang has already telegraphed Hubei, instructing Meng Guangpeng, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, to temporarily act as chairman. As for the criminal Cheng Xiechao, who was stabbed, after several strict interrogations, his confession is still flickering. He was transferred to the Army Prison on the 27th to await a joint trial by a special military court formed by various agencies. It is said that he will be transferred to the Central Government for questioning. Of the suspects arrested, five were released on bail on the 26th, but it is reported that several others have been arrested and are still being detained awaiting interrogation. (October 27th)

Strange Behavior of Taiwanese People Outside the South Gate of Quanzhou: Using Magic Shows and Selling Medicine for Propaganda; A Certain Foreigner Probes the Situation in Shishi 73

Xiamen Correspondence: In Shishi and the coastal area outside the South Gate of Quanzhou, certain figures have been very active recently. A few days ago, in the Linkou Township area, a number of Taiwanese suddenly appeared, disguised as street performers doing magic tricks and selling plaster. They went deep into the countryside, acting strangely. They carried two cloth-made dragon flags with the words "National Salvation Corps" written on them. They beat drums and gongs to attract ordinary villagers and engaged in extensive propaganda. They first started by talking about Zheng Chenggong's resistance against the Qing Dynasty in Taiwan, and then praised Japan's wealth and strength, and finally talked about the necessity of cooperation between China and Japan. They traveled around various villages and made the same arguments everywhere, while the business of selling plaster seemed insignificant. Moreover, although Shishi is an important commercial and transportation hub in southern Fujian, it is by no means a scenic spot. Four foreigners (including one woman) who did not carry passports also traveled to Shishi and the surrounding villages the other day. Among them, there were those who could speak the Southern Min dialect and specialized in questioning ignorant villagers about the local situation and writing it down in books. It can be said that they must have a purpose. (October 28th)

The Headquarters for the Suppression of Bandits in the Border Area of Fujian, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Anhui Moves to Quzhou; All Sectors in Jiangshan Hold a Grand Farewell Party; Zhang Fakui Delivers a Reply, Encouraging Efforts in Construction 74

Jiangshan Correspondence: Since the headquarters of the General Commander for the Suppression of Bandits in the border area of the four provinces of Fujian, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Anhui has been stationed in Jiangshan, eight months have passed in an instant. During this period, General Commander Zhang Fakui, in addition to earnestly engaging in the suppression of remnant bandits, has also actively promoted and spared no effort in all local construction. The most prominent achievements include the implementation of compulsory literacy education for the masses, the construction of Zhongshan and Zhongzheng Avenues, and the rigorous implementation of the New Life Movement, which has transformed the old Jiangshan, which was filled with apathy, into a new Jiangshan full of vitality. Recently, in order to facilitate the command and suppression of bandits, the headquarters moved to Quzhou. The local people of this county, having heard the news beforehand, tried unsuccessfully to persuade them to stay. Therefore, at 8:00 AM on the 26th of the month, the "Jiangshan All Sectors Farewell General Commander Zhang's Departure to Sanqu Farewell Commemorative Meeting" was held at the Public Gymnasium in the city to express their thoughts. On that day, more than a hundred groups from Party, government, military, agriculture, industry, commerce, and education, and more than ten thousand people participated. General Commander Zhang and all the officers and soldiers of the headquarters arrived on time. The military band played loudly. First, the presidium and representatives of various groups delivered speeches, unanimously praising General Commander Zhang's efforts in suppressing bandits, his strict discipline in governing the army, and his enthusiasm for construction over the past eight months, expressing their intention not to forget his prestige. Then, they presented embroidered flags with the words "Guardian of the Country," "Meritorious Deeds in the Party-State," "Guaranteeing the Southeast," and "Benefiting the People of Jiang" to commemorate him. Then, General Commander Zhang delivered a reply, saying that in the past eight months, he had asked himself whether he had made many contributions to the Party-State and the local area. However, he was so warmly welcomed by the elders of all sectors in Jiangshan, which he did not dare to take. Now, based on the meaning of the ancient farewell remarks, he hoped that the Jiangshan compatriots would unite in spirit, cooperate with each other, and build a new Jiangshan as the foundation for the future revival of the Chinese nation. His words were very alert, and the whole scene was moved. Finally, all the people formed a team to go to the bus station outside the South Gate to see him off, and set off firecrackers all the way. The situation was extremely warm.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Strictly Prohibits the Private Export of Foodstuffs; Sea Transport Requires Passports; County Governments Responsible for Inspection 75

Zhenjiang Correspondence: Since the beginning of autumn, although Jiangsu Province has had a bumper harvest of food crops, prices have soared. It is believed that the main reasons are the private export of food by grain merchants and hoarding for profit. Ordinary people are suffering immensely. In order to maintain the people's food supply, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has specially formulated the "Provisional Measures for Strictly Prohibiting the Export of Foodstuffs from Jiangsu Province," which was passed at the Provincial Government meeting on the 27th. The details are recorded as follows: (1) These provisional measures are specially formulated in order to maintain the people's food supply in this province. (2) Foodstuffs from various counties in this province are allowed to circulate freely, except for transportation that requires a passport for sea transport. The aforementioned passports shall be issued by the county government where the business firm purchasing the foodstuffs is located. No fees shall be charged for passports. (3) If other provinces or cities report a need and are approved by the provincial government for assistance, the provincial government shall issue a passport for the grain to leave the province. The county government at the place of exit shall verify the compliance before allowing it to pass; otherwise, it will be considered private export. (4) County governments of counties along the Yangtze River, along the coast, and bordering neighboring provinces are responsible for inspecting foodstuffs leaving the territory. However, they must not deliberately create difficulties, extort money, or engage in favoritism. Violations will result in severe punishment for the responsible officials and strict legal action against all other personnel involved. (5) Anyone who encounters food from this province being privately transported out to sea at various ports along the Yangtze River and along the coast can report it to the local government or maritime customs office to intercept it. (6) If a rice merchant is found to be privately exporting foodstuffs to sea, in addition to confiscating the foodstuffs, they will also be ordered to suspend their business operations. (7) For foodstuffs seized during private exports to sea or out of the province, if the quantity is below 50 shi, all shall be used as rewards; if it is between 50 shi and 100 shi, 50% shall be used as rewards, and the remaining 50% shall be transferred to the Food Management Committee for storage; if it is above 100 shi, one-quarter shall be used as rewards, and the remaining three-quarters shall be transferred to the Food Management Committee for storage. (8) The rewarded foodstuffs shall be distributed with 60% going to the informer and 40% to the local government or customs office that accepted the report and intercepted the goods. (9) If a person reports the private export of foodstuffs to sea or out of the province with malicious intent, they shall be severely punished according to the law once verified. (10) These provisional measures shall be implemented upon deliberation and promulgation by the Provincial Government Committee.

Suzhou: A Boat Sailing from Dongshan Robbed by Bandits 76

Recently, bandits have run rampant in the Suzhou countryside, and robberies are frequently heard. Farmers in the four villages cannot sleep peacefully. A few days ago, major robbery cases occurred in Zhouzhuang and other villages, and the authorities are strictly investigating. Unexpectedly, a boat sailing from Dongting Dongshan to Huzhou in Zhejiang Province encountered another bandit boat with more than ten bandits carrying weapons on the 27th while passing through Jueshan in Taihu Lake. All passengers on board were robbed, losing more than 500 yuan. The bandits fled to the lake area of Huzhou in Zhejiang Province. On the same day, robberies of boats also occurred near Dongshan, but the losses were minimal. The Second District Commissioner's Office convened a water and public security meeting of the eight counties on the 28th to discuss the Taihu Lake bandits. With the approach of winter prevention, it will join the Zhejiang Provincial water and land teams to conduct a large-scale encirclement and suppression to maintain security in the four villages.

Wuxi: The Surge in Cotton Yarn Prices Has Subsided 77

The market price of cotton yarn in this city soared in the past week due to brisk sales. Recently, foreign cotton has not improved, and the price surge has subsided. Market sentiment has also become sluggish. Yesterday, the price of various brands of cotton yarn fell by several jiao to two yuan per piece. It is predicted that there is still a possibility of further price declines in the future market. Furthermore, it is learned that the market situation for rice and paddy in this city has also declined by about one jiao per dan due to a surge in arrivals and sluggish sales. Clear white japonica rice is priced at 9.2 yuan. However, some merchants are still shipping rice and grain abroad, and it is hoped that the authorities will stop this to maintain the people's food supply. It is reported that 200 rice boats were intercepted at the junction of Wuxi and Jiangyin a few days ago.

Establishment of a Health Office 78

The county government of this city is planning to establish a county-wide health office, which County Magistrate Long is actively pursuing. The first preparatory meeting was convened yesterday and resolved the following: (1) It will have three sections: General Affairs, Architectural Design, and Construction. Li Shouxuan was appointed as the head of the General Affairs section, Zhang Fulin as the head of the Architectural Design section, and Wu Yifeng as the head of the Construction section. (2) There are currently two types of organizational systems for the Health Office. Mountain Consultant Weng Zhilong, Zai Yuanchen, and Committee Member Wu Yifeng will jointly discuss and review them. (3) The number of staff will be reviewed by the previous case review committee. (4) In addition to allocating 18,800 yuan specifically for equipment costs, the remaining funds will be used for construction costs. It is estimated that at least an additional 10,000 yuan will be needed to meet the needs, which will be submitted to the province for approval. (5) The establishment expenses for the Health Office and the County Hospital have been approved. The allocation ratio for each item will be reviewed by Consultants Weng and Wang, and Committee Member Wu. It was also decided to build the location near Deyuan Road in Ximen. Once the blueprint is finalized, bidding can be invited for construction.

Changshu: Death from Crab Poisoning 79

Yesterday, a person in the Xixu town of this place suddenly died of crab poisoning. Zhao Meixuan from Yangshe went to Qian Yixing's southern goods store in Xushi the day before yesterday to collect payments. Because Mr. Qian and Mr. Zhao were old friends, Qian entertained Zhao with a large crab before dinner, and they ate it together. Unexpectedly, Zhao was already ill. Because he liked crabs very much, he ate four or five in a row. At the time, there was nothing unusual, but at midnight, he had severe abdominal pain and died at dawn. Therefore, Mr. Qian was greatly shocked and sent someone to quickly report to his family to collect the body.

Septuagenarian Old Man Takes a New Bride 80

Zhuang Liangxian, the head of the Xizhang Township, is 75 years old this year. He owns three to four thousand mu of fertile land and is the richest man in the entire township. Mr. Zhuang has married three wives, who have passed away one after another. He has two sons and two daughters, the oldest of whom is thirty years old and the youngest still a child. This spring, Mr. Zhuang, feeling lonely in his solitary residence, met Ms. Gui Yuejing, a female teacher at a certain school, who is 31 years old this year. Zhuang immediately asked someone to act as an intermediary and hired her as his next wife with 1,400 yuan in cash and 1,000 mu of fertile land. They were engaged in July, but unexpectedly, his eldest son and brother-in-law (former wife) opposed it and blocked its progress. Both parties sued in the county judiciary. Zhuang was once detained, causing the rice stored at home to be stolen and sold. The lawsuit is still ongoing. However, Mr. Zhuang's marriage is still his intention and continues to proceed. On the 27th, he held a wedding ceremony with Ms. Gui at his residence outside the East Gate. Lawyers Yu Chengmei and He Baoshu were hired to witness the marriage. White hair and a red face became a good story for a while. Later, according to the septuagenarian groom's public statement, "Although there is an age difference between my wife and me, there are no regulations in law." In other words, it is legal. "However, my marriage is not for the sake of succession. I already have children and grandchildren, so it is out of the question. However, in my own life, I have a companion." After he finished speaking, everyone laughed.

Nantong: Dissolution of the Private Investigation Intelligence Office 81

The Ministry of Finance's pilot Tong-Ru-Chong-Hai District Investigation Smuggling Intelligence Office was ineffective and had many drawbacks. The Ministry of Finance has ordered it to stop its activities and dismissed the staff that day. It also notified the public security bureaus of various counties that if there are still people outside engaging in activities claiming to be from the office, they are falsely using the name and should be arrested.

Yangzhou: Protecting the Dikes Along the Canal 82

The Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau stated that the dikes on the east and west banks of the various counties along the canal are densely populated with shops and residents. According to the ban on building houses on the canal dikes, they should all be demolished. However, the method of gradually abolishing them was determined, but people still arbitrarily abused them, which greatly hindered the dike construction. It is urgent to strictly ban them. The county government of this county yesterday received an order to be responsible for protecting the dike works on the east and west banks of the towns along the canal. It is strictly forbidden for merchants and residents living in the towns along the dikes to damage the top and body of the dikes, dump garbage, or dig dike soil, resulting in the increasing incompleteness of the dike body and dike slope. After this prohibition, if the above situation occurs again, the township heads will report to the county to arrest and severely punish those responsible.

Gaoyou: Managing All Hotels in the City 83

There are more than 50 hotels in this city. In the winter of 1932, the county government formulated rules for managing hotel operations and issued business licenses, which has been more than three years. The county government, in view of the imminent arrival of winter prevention and the extremely tense situation, believes that some unscrupulous hotels may harbor dirt and filth and easily allow bandits to hide and harm the local area. In order to maintain local stability, it has re-formulated management rules and exchanged business licenses. New ones cost two yuan each, plus five jiao for stamp duty; exchanges cost one yuan, plus five jiao for stamp duty. It has also issued a public announcement.

Haizhou: Food Prices in the Coastal Areas Soar 84

Although the autumn harvest of food crops in the coastal areas this year has been greatly reduced compared with previous years, it is still sufficient to supply the local people if there are no unscrupulous merchants manipulating purchases and exports. However, in recent months, a certain country has used unscrupulous merchants to purchase food in large quantities in various parts of the coastal areas, transporting it by rail and shipping it, amounting to thousands of bags a day, causing food prices to rise several times a day. Taking Song flour as an example, the value of each bag was only 3.4 yuan last month, but now it has risen to 4.05 yuan. The prices of other various foods have also risen by 30% to 40%. The general public is crying bitterly. In the blink of an eye, the severe winter of ice and snow will arrive. If the authorities do not find a way to ban exports, the food supply in the coastal areas will be even more unimaginable.

Woodcutter Kills Giant Snake 85

Zhang Kaibang, a resident of the Seventh Bao of Lugou Township, Lianyungang City, is over 30 years old and earns a living as a woodcutter. Because the firewood and grass in the nearby mountains have been almost exhausted, he discussed with his neighbor Cheng Sen and others to go to distant places to cut grass. Yesterday morning, at the time of the rooster crowing, Kaibang got up and entered the mountain. Cheng and others also followed him into the mountain. While Cheng and others were walking, they suddenly heard Kaibang calling for help in front of them and shouting "Snake!" Cheng and others rushed forward and saw a giant snake, about two zhang long, with blue scales, bright and dazzling. The snake's tail was wrapped around Kaibang's body. Seeing this, Cheng and others used shoulder poles and sickles to kill the snake and carried Kaibang to a nearby farmer's house. After washing his face with clean water, he was able to speak. According to experts, the snake is called a grass snake and does not bite. It has two whiskers. It coils around people, uses its whiskers to probe people's nostrils, and sucks their brains, causing them to die immediately. The whole snake weighed 96 jin. Farmers who heard the news came to watch in an endless stream.

Ningbo: Mega-Swindler Xie Zhiqing Arrested 86

Xie Zhiqing, a businessman at No. 106 Dongjiao Road, this port, had a whimsical idea in September 1933. He falsely set up a business name, fraudulently obtained goods from various stores, and transported them to Yuyao for sale. After the deception was discovered, he fled without a trace. Those who were defrauded included Xin Kang's salted goods store for more than 450 yuan, Wan Shunhao for more than 200 yuan, Runshenghao for more than 300 yuan, and Yuan Xin Hao for 330 yuan. The Criminal Investigation Team investigated the case. The swindler Xie Zhiqing recently appeared in Ningbo and was reported to the court by Xie Dechen, the owner of Xin Kanghao, for detention. Such a mega-swindling case in Ningbo is rare in recent years.

Education News

National Higher Education: The Number of Full-Time Teachers Has Increased 87

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the increase and decrease of full-time and part-time teachers in national colleges and universities. The results are as follows:

(1) In the 20th year, among the 7,5-- teachers in national colleges and universities, 4,133 were full-time, accounting for 58.60%, and 2,920 were part-time with external positions, accounting for 41.40%. (2) In the 21st year, among the 6,709 people, 4,723 were full-time, accounting for 70.43%. The number of part-time internal positions increased by 592, an increase of 11.83%. There were 1,984 part-time external positions, accounting for 29.97% of the total, a decrease of 936 people compared with the previous part-time external positions, accounting for 11.83%. (3) In the 22nd year, among the 7,200 people, 5,000 were full-time, accounting for 69.49%. The number of part-time internal positions increased by 867, an increase of 10.89%. There were 2,100 part-time external positions, accounting for 30.55%, a decrease of 720 people compared with the previous 20th year, a decrease of 10.85%. (4) In the 23rd year, among the 7,205 people, 5,127 were full-time, accounting for 71.16%. The number of part-time internal positions increased by 994, an increase of 12.56%. There were 1,078 part-time external positions, accounting for 28.84%, a decrease of 842 people compared with the 20th year, and the percentage also increased by 12.96%. From this, it can be seen that the number of teachers in national higher education who previously held part-time external positions has been decreasing year by year, and the number of those who are full-time and part-time internal positions has been increasing.

This Year's Measures by the Ministry of Education to Subsidize Hardworking Students from the Northeast 88

The Shanghai social sector yesterday ordered public and private secondary schools and private colleges and universities, saying, "The Ministry of Education's Northeast Youth Education Relief Office's telegram stated that the office's subsidies for Northeast students in 1940 were previously reviewed and processed by sending the regulations, nomination forms, deadline for nominations, and notes. However, the Northeast students of all levels of schools have claimed that they did not understand the meaning of the free quota and public expense quota programs promulgated by the Ministry, mistakenly believing that applying for a certificate of poverty could obtain the subsidy from the office, resulting in a lack of nominations. It would be a pity if they lost the opportunity to receive a subsidy because of this. Please find a way to remedy it. Therefore, the office affairs meeting resolved: (1) The deadline for schools at all levels in all provinces and cities to nominate hardworking students from the Northeast is extended to the end of this year. Those who have sent the nomination documents to the office and declared that they will submit the missing documents are also limited to submit them before the end of October. No extensions will be granted to ensure the integrity of official duties. (2) In the future, if Northeast students in various schools apply for a certificate of poverty, the schools should first assess them. If it is confirmed that they are poor and have lived in a place for less than three years (those who have lived in a place for three years should apply to the local competent educational administrative agency), and the school has free and public expense quotas according to the regulations, the school will forward them to the office for verification. The office will no longer directly accept applications. Those who mistakenly believe that applying for a certificate of poverty can obtain the subsidy from the office should be explained by the schools to avoid misunderstandings. In addition to sending telegrams, this is hereby sent to you for your information and to inform all schools under your jurisdiction. This is a public friendship." Therefore, after reviewing the case, the city Education Bureau received the regulations and forms sent by the Northeast Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry of Education and ordered them to be followed. Now, according to the previous, it is ordered to be informed of this order.

Status of National Academic Institutions and Organizations 90

The Ministry of Education recently compiled statistics on national academic institutions and organizations, which have increased year by year. Before the founding of the Republic of China, there were only five. From the first year of the Republic of China to the third year, there were six each year. In the fourth year, there were ten; in the fifth year, there were thirteen; in the sixth year, there were fourteen; from the first year of the Republic of China to the tenth year, there were seventeen each year; in the eleventh year, there were twenty-one; in the twelfth year, there were twenty-three; in the thirteenth year, there were twenty; in the fourteenth year, there were thirty; in the fifteenth year, there were thirty-seven; in the sixteenth year, there were forty-five; in the seventeenth year, there were fifty-four; in the sixteenth year, there were seventy; in the nineteenth year, there were eighty-six; in the twentieth year, there were ninety-six; in the twenty-first year, there were one hundred and thirteen; in the twenty-second year, there were one hundred and twenty-eight; and in the twenty-third year, there were one hundred and forty-four. Among them, there are 35 academic institutions and 109 academic organizations. Among these 109, there are 22 general categories, 7 sports categories, 34 practical categories (8 science, 4 agriculture and forestry, 10 engineering, 12 medicine), and 46 literature categories (8 literature and art, 22 social sciences, 16 education). The academic institutions and organizations are distributed as follows: 56 in the capital city, 36 in Shanghai, 14 in Beiping, ten in Jiangsu, six in Fujian, and three each in Guo and Jie. There are one each in Zhejiang, Hebei, Qing (Dao), Hunan, Shandong, Shanxi, and Sui, and one each in Anhui, Henan, Guangdong, Guizhou, and Wei. According to their distribution, the capital city has the most, ranking first, Shanghai ranks second, and Beiping ranks third. Among the 35 major academic institutions in the country, such as the National Central Research Institute, the Beiping Research Institute, the National Compilation and Translation Bureau, the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, and the Geological Survey of the Ministry of Industry, all occupy important positions in the academic community. The remaining ones are newly established, provincial, or municipal. Their total annual expenditure is more than 4.6 million yuan, and their annual income is more than 4.48 million yuan (the annual income of the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center is 480,000, and the annual expenditure is 550,000; the annual income of the Central Guoshu Hall is 60,000, and the annual expenditure is 70,000; the annual income of the Forensic Medical Institute is 3,000, and the annual expenditure is 66,000, all of which are insufficient to cover expenses). The equipment status is mainly divided into instruments, specimens, books, medicines, and special equipment. The personnel are divided into staff and researchers, full-time staff of more than 260, full-time researchers of more than 250, part-time staff of more than 140, part-time researchers of more than 180, staff of more than 550 who are not divided into part-time, and researchers of more than 509. A total of 262 research projects have been completed, and 331 are still in progress. A total of 507 publications have been published, including 128 series, 27 periodicals, and 352 other reports and special publications. The national academic and health organizations total 109, with an annual income of more than 786,000 yuan and an annual expenditure of 769,000 yuan. There are more than 2,700 staff members and 52,900 members, including more than 1,780 new members. There are more than 980 publications, totaling 3,399, including 84 periodicals and 501 other magazines, reports, and special publications. The increase in academic institutions and organizations over the years has been most vigorous since the establishment of the National Government in 1927, which can be called the most prosperous era in the 20 years since the founding of the Republic of China.

Qinghai Students Come to Shanghai to Study 92

Twelve arrived here yesterday

Qinghai is located in a remote area with blocked transportation. There are almost no students studying in Shanghai. Chen Hecen, Liu Zhanen, Shu Xincheng, He Qingxu, and other members of the Frontier Education Committee of the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Education Society are concerned about this. They worked with the New Qinghai Society to find ways for Qinghai youths to study in practice to prepare for the development of the frontier. The New Qinghai Society specially sent Zhang Deshan, director of the editorial department, to Shanghai to contact Chen, Liu, Shu, and others. As a result, eleven Qinghai students were recruited and subsidized for food and accommodation to study in Shanghai. The Qinghai Provincial Education Association and the New Qinghai Society jointly undertook the recruitment. A total of eleven students were recruited and arrived in Beijing at 8:00 a.m. on the 26th of this month. They took a train to Shanghai at 12:25 p.m. on the 27th, led by Zhang Deshan, director of the editorial department of the New Qinghai Society. They arrived here at 9:00 p.m. that afternoon. The Shanghai Society reporter specially visited Mr. Zhang to inquire about the details.

Recruitment Process

For the sake of prudence in this recruitment, Yang Xiyao and Gu Huaifeng of the Qinghai Provincial Education Association and Deng Qinyi and Ma Zunwei of the New Qinghai Society agreed on the recruitment method on August 20. They immediately posted recruitment advertisements, underwent written tests and physical examinations, and completed the process on August 28, enrolling twelve students.

Route

The students were all going out for the first time and were not familiar with transportation. Led by Ma Lingwei, director of the General Affairs Department of the New Qinghai Society, they set off from Xining on September 5 and arrived in Lanzhou on the 10th. Unfortunately, the Red bandits blocked the road, and the Xilan Road was blocked. After waiting until the 17th, they decided to take rafts along the Yellow River on the 27th. After passing through the Sangye Gorge, Boiling Man Pot, Dazhaobi, Xiaozhaobi, Yin and Yang , and other dangerous places, they traveled by water for ten days and arrived in Ningxia on October 10. There was a tense suppression of bandits in Ningxia. After waiting for four days, they took a boat on October 16 and traveled day and night, arriving in Baotou on the 18th. They took a car to Ban at 5:00 p.m. that evening. Due to the hardship of the journey, they rested for three days and took the Pingpu car at 9:00 a.m. on the 24th, arriving in Beijing on the 26th. This time, they received a lot of help from Acting Chairman Ma Bufang, Director Yang Xiyao, Gansu Pacification Director Zhu Yimin, and Chief Li Shijun of the 29th Army, making the journey much easier. They arrived in Shanghai by car at 12:25 p.m. today. Although the students have been through a long journey, they are all in good spirits and there were no accidents along the way.

Final Thoughts

Finally, Mr. Zhang said that the Qinghai students were warmly welcomed in Shanghai during the 6th National Games last year, and their spirits were greatly lifted. Many are willing to come to Shanghai to learn applied science and plan to build the frontier. This decision has also been promoted by the educational circles in Shanghai, which is deeply appreciated. Qinghai is located in the remote northwest and is an important strategic location for national defense. Therefore, the responsibility of Qinghai youths is great. I hope that people from all walks of life in Shanghai will provide more assistance so that aspiring youths can have the opportunity to study and develop their abilities, and the entire Qinghai people will benefit greatly. In addition, it was originally planned to recruit two female students to study midwifery, but unfortunately, the older female students in Qinghai cannot leave their environment, and the younger ones are inconvenient to manage, and their families are not at ease. Therefore, they could not be recruited. However, there are many who are willing to come to Shanghai to study, so we have to wait for the future. The list of students is as follows:

General Education Overview (1) 93

— Lei Zhen

(Lecture at the Employment Guidance Class for Colleges and Above)

Hello everyone, today I will be talking to you about the current state of education in our country, which I will divide into four parts: (1) the state of elementary education nationwide, (2) the state of secondary education nationwide, (3) the state of higher education nationwide, and (4) the state of social education nationwide.

(1) The State of Elementary Education Nationwide Elementary education is the lowest level of education in the educational system. Elementary institutions can be roughly divided into two types: "kindergartens" and "primary schools."

Kindergartens are for children who have not yet reached the age of primary school enrollment, that is, children aged four to six, and provide them with education. The most important purpose of establishing kindergartens is to use various games and activities to teach young children, based on their natural inclination to move and love being in groups, to strengthen their bodies, exercise their senses, and increase their ability to observe and organize. This is a common need for all young children, especially for mothers who are busy with work and have no time to take care of their children, or for families that lack the knowledge and experience to care for young children. It would be more appropriate to send the young children to kindergartens. The number of kindergartens in our country is very small. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there were a total of 1,097 kindergartens nationwide, with only 47,512 children. Although there has been progress in each year, the gap with actual needs is still very large. Among these 40,000+ children, boys account for about 57.7%, and girls account for about 43.3%. The male to female ratio is very close. Equal educational opportunities for men and women in our country can only be勉强talked about in kindergartens. The rest of the general primary, secondary schools, and universities are not as good. In terms of preschool education, this is a somewhat comforting thing.

Now, let's talk about primary schools. Primary schools are the place where compulsory national education is implemented. The duration of study is six years. The first four years are junior primary school, and the last two years are senior primary school. Junior primary schools can be established independently. Before education is universalized, junior primary school is the minimum compulsory education that citizens should receive. All children who are six years old must enter junior primary school. In special circumstances, they may be extended to nine years old. According to regulations, primary schools should not charge tuition fees in principle. In situations where local areas have no choice, they may also collect fees as appropriate. In public primary schools, the maximum fee per person per semester should not exceed one yuan for junior grades and two yuan for senior grades. In private primary schools, the maximum fee per person per semester should not exceed three yuan for junior grades and six yuan for senior grades. Primary schools that charge tuition fees should have one-third or more of their student body enrolled as poor children who receive free tuition. If a student cannot afford to pay tuition, the primary school principal should consider the situation and waive part or all of the tuition.

The length of compulsory education varies from country to country. For example, it is six years in Japan, seven years or more in the United States, eight years in Germany, France, and Belgium, and nine years or more in the United Kingdom, while it is only four years in our country. Even with these short four years, many children cannot attend school because of poverty. Even if they have enrolled, they still cannot finish their education. Therefore, in order to promote the popularization of compulsory education, the Ministry of Education has, on the one hand, urged local areas to widely establish the aforementioned senior and junior primary schools, and on the other hand, stipulated that local areas may establish simplified primary schools and short-term primary schools to provide assistance. Each province and city should handle various types of primary schools according to local conditions, and people are free to choose a suitable primary school and enroll their children, so that all citizens can receive the minimum compulsory education. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there were a total of 257,998 primary schools nationwide, including 208,009 junior primary schools, 22,319 primary schools that jointly operate both junior and senior grades, 4,044 simplified primary schools, 2,603 short-term primary schools, and 623 other types of schools. There were a total of 12,335,967 primary school students, including 11,083,253 junior primary school students, 1,066,955 senior primary school students, 82,180 simplified primary school students, 84,511 short-term primary school students, and 19,068 other students. There are about 27 primary school students for every thousand people. The children receiving compulsory education actually account for less than 25% of school-age children, which is much lower than the advanced countries where education has been popularized. It is also inferior to modern emerging countries such as Poland, Turkey, and Soviet Russia, because the number of children enrolled in their schools has generally reached more than 90% of school-age children.

In the 24th year of the Republic (1935), the Ministry of Education, in accordance with the Fourth Central Executive Committee's Fifth Plenary Session's plan to implement compulsory education, both as a stopgap measure and a fundamental solution, formulated a ten-year plan for compulsory education, namely the Outline of Temporary Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education, which was announced last year. Its implementation procedure is divided into three phases:

The first phase is from August of the 24th year of the Republic (1935) to July of the 29th year of the Republic (1940). In addition to expanding existing primary schools, a large number of one-year short-term primary schools will be established. In the last year of this phase, namely the 29th year of the Republic (1940), at least 80% of school-age children nationwide should receive at least one year of short-term primary school education. The second phase is from August of the 29th year of the Republic (1940) to July of the 33rd year of the Republic (1944). During this phase, one-year short-term primary schools will be gradually converted into two-year short-term primary schools. In the last year of this phase, namely the 33rd year of the Republic (1944), at least 80% of school-age children nationwide should receive at least two years of short-term primary school education.

The third phase is from August of the 33rd year of the Republic (1944). Two-year short-term primary schools should be gradually converted into four-year junior primary schools, so that all school-age children nationwide receive at least four years of compulsory education.

The current one-year short-term primary schools enroll children aged nine to twelve and provide them with instruction in the national language, arithmetic, civics, and physical education. Tuition is free, and students' school supplies are also provided free of charge by the school. Those who should enroll but do not will first have their parents or elder brothers persuaded to allow them to enroll. If, after repeated persuasion, they still do not allow their children to enroll, they will be fined one to five yuan and still be ordered to allow their children to enroll.

However, in order to implement this ten-year plan for compulsory education, it is first necessary to prepare funding. In the past, the slow progress of compulsory education was due to financial difficulties, which was a major reason. When formulating the ten-year plan this time, in addition to ordering provinces and cities to raise funds on their own, the central government also allocated funds to subsidize them. In the 24th year of the Republic (1935), the central government subsidized provinces and cities with 3.2 million yuan. In the 25th year of the Republic (1936), this was increased to 4.75 million yuan, and it is planned to gradually increase this amount in the future. At the same time, provinces and cities are also urged to gradually raise more funds, in the hope that the promotion of compulsory education will not be delayed due to financial difficulties.

With funding secured, the Ministry of Education, on the one hand, (1) established the National Compulsory Education Committee of the Ministry of Education to assist in the national compulsory education, (2) reviewed the income and expenditure of compulsory education funds in various provinces and cities, and (3) appointed supervisors to go to various provinces and cities to inspect, urge, and provide guidance. On the other hand, (1) it issued a notice to all provinces and cities to formulate and determine plans for the implementation of compulsory education, (2) it issued a notice to all provinces and cities to organize provincial and county compulsory education committees to assist the competent educational administrative organs of the provinces, counties, and cities in handling compulsory education, and (3) it issued a notice to all provinces and cities to divide primary school districts, dividing each district into approximately one thousand households, and actively engaging in the establishment of short-term primary schools. In recent years, a total of 48,000 short-term primary schools and 16,000 short-term primary school classes have been added nationwide, with more than 4 million students. This year, in order to promote the work of compulsory education in various provinces and cities, the Ministry of Education has specially organized a training class for compulsory education cadres in Beijing. 各省市recommendedrelevant personnel to come to Beijing for training. This training has now begun. In the future, after the trainees return to their provinces, they will be responsible for training compulsory education personnel in the counties and cities, so that the personnel engaged in compulsory education work can clearly understand and implement all laws, regulations, and procedures. (To be continued)

Basketball Friendly Match: Xin Team Wins Against American Military 105

75 to 33

The Xin Team basketball team, in preparation for participating in the West Youth League, played a friendly match yesterday against the American Navy's "奥搿司脫" Fleet at the Sichuan Road Navy Youth Association gymnasium. The match was divided into four quarters. In the first quarter, the American military showed great vigor, tying the score at 13-12, which surprised the audience. By the end of the first half, the Xin Team had already taken a seven-point lead. In the third and fourth quarters, the American soldiers' momentum changed drastically, and they were defeated in a landslide. The final result was 75 to 33, with the Xin Team winning decisively. However, the little fat man Xu Zhaoxiong did not play; otherwise, the record would have been even more impressive.

Recent Overview of Sports in the Soviet Union (Continued from Yesterday) 109

— Song Ruhai

From the perspective of this type of sports program, it can be seen that Soviet Russia uses all-around sports methods to promote sports among the people. Members of various groups who pass the exam are awarded certificates and medals by the central government. Those who pass the first-level exam must continue training for one year before they can take the first-level exam. The second-level sports standard includes 24 items, including physiology, hygiene, and sports theory. Those who obtain the second level can enjoy the rights of various sports associations and can directly enter sports schools. In 1935, there were 10,000 people nationwide who obtained the first-level award. By the summer of 1926, this had increased to more than 3.6 million people. There were 5,000 people who obtained the second-level award, including 200 women. 600,000 children obtained the Dyamo award. According to national statistics, approximately 8.71 million people participated in sports, with women accounting for one-third. In the past two years, approximately 200 sports fields have been built in various cities, schools, factories, military camps, etc. In the Soviet Union's second five-year plan, physical education is the main undertaking for training the people. Therefore, special attention is paid to the planning and design of training sports instructors. There are currently four vocational schools specializing in physical education, with more than 4,000 male and female students. In the past three years, 20 physical education secondary schools have been added, with 4,200 male and female students. In addition, 25 physical education departments have been attached to various normal schools, with more than 2,900 students. In total, there are more than 10,000 people studying physical education. In 1935, the graduates from various levels of schools were: (A) 415 physical education specialists, (B) 476 secondary physical education school graduates, (C) more than 900 graduates from normal school affiliated departments, (D) approximately 2,000 people from special physical education training classes. According to the statistics of the Central Sports Commission, there are currently 20,000 people serving in the sports field nationwide. (To be continued)

Chengdu-Chongqing Railway Funding Agreed Upon 115

French Banking Consortium and Others Cooperate on Investment - Wei Wenbin and Others Return to Shanghai from Sichuan

Shun Shi News Agency reports that regarding the funding for the construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway, since an agreement was reached on joint investment by the China Construction Bank Corporation and a French banking consortium, Deng Yiguang, Director of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway Engineering Office, and others came to Shanghai in early this month to negotiate the details. On the 18th of this month, Deng Yiguang, Director of the Engineering Office, along with Wei Wenbin, representative of the Construction Bank Corporation, and Fran冯丹, representative of the French banking consortium, flew to Chengdu to estimate the cost of materials for the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway project and inspect the entire project. It is learned that Wei Wenbin, representative of the Construction Bank Corporation, and Fran冯丹, representative of the French banking consortium, completed their task the day before yesterday and returned to Shanghai via Nanjing. The valuation of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway project materials has been completed. In terms of funding, in addition to the investment by the French banking consortium, the Chinese side will cooperate with the Construction Bank Corporation, the financial sector, and the Sichuan Provincial Government. The details of the participation have also been agreed upon.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce National Exhibition and National Products Market - Amount of Donations from One-Day Campaign 117

The National Products Exhibition of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, located at 126 Jing'an Temple Road, and the National Products Market on North Henan Road are both organized by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Since the Chamber agreed to the "One-Day Contribution to the Nation" campaign initiated by the Li Bao newspaper, all 89 manufacturers participating in the exhibition and the market unanimously complied with the announcement and implemented the campaign on October 26th, donating all of the day's business income to the purchase of airplanes for birthday celebrations. It is learned that on that day, the total business of the exhibition, such as Tiger Balm Wing On Hall, was 334.439 yuan, Anmian Si Mattress Factory was 108 yuan, Renfeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory was 67.72 yuan, Anle Plush Factory was 37.88 yuan, and Meiya Silk Weaving Factory was 37.4 yuan. In the National Products Market, Hongzhang Textile Dyeing Factory was 129.77 yuan, Huahua Silk Company was 41.21 yuan, Huahua Store was 21.57 yuan, and Xiangxing Leather Factory was 14.21 yuan. In total, the business of the two locations reached nearly 1,000 yuan, which has been remitted to the Finance Section of the City Chamber of Commerce for collection over the past two days and forwarded to the Airplane Purchase Birthday Celebration Committee. In addition, the Special Industry Association, under the responsibility of Mr. Du Yuesheng, is raising 100,000 yuan to purchase a "Shanghai Anti-Smoking" airplane. Yesterday, Mr. Du sent Mr. Wan Molin to pay 20,000 yuan in donations to the Airplane Purchase Commemoration Committee for counting. The committee also received 580 yuan donated by all officers and soldiers of the 339th Regiment of the 169th Brigade of the 57th Division of the Army, (original letter attached), 10 yuan from Yida Tea Box Lead Factory, 15 yuan from all workers who deliver mail to the Japanese Consulate, 20 yuan from ten Chinese drivers of the Japanese Consulate such as Yao Changqing, 29.4 yuan from Shangcai Primary School, and 10 yuan from Li Shaofang. Receipts have been issued to Liu Yi. In addition, the Ximen Huangjiaguan Road branch of Rendeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory will hold a "One-Day Contribution to the Nation" event on the 30th of this month, selling various goods, limited to retail (wholesale is an exception), with a 20% discount off the original price to show sacrifice, in order to increase the quantity and present it to the government for the purchase of airplanes for birthday celebrations. It is expected that the store will be extremely crowded on that day. The original letter from the 339th Regiment of officers and soldiers is recorded as follows: To the Shanghai Newspaper Office, Having learned of the "One-Day Contribution to the Nation" campaign initiated by the Shanghai business, academic, and other circles, we are deeply impressed. We soldiers are the vanguard of the people, and we are willing to sacrifice our families and lives. How dare we lag behind in contributing the income of just one day to the nation? Therefore, although the entire division has already donated funds to purchase airplanes, we still cannot control our feelings. The entire regiment of officers and soldiers has decided to donate one day's salary, totaling 580 yuan, to the nation to celebrate the birthday of the Chairman. In addition to collecting the funds for remittance, we hope that all compatriots in the country and armed comrades will respond together, and that colleagues in the press will strongly promote it, so that we can gather strength and increase official strength. The nation and the nation will greatly benefit from it. This is respectfully reported, and we wish you peace. Famous American Fisheries Expert Mr. Hai Lai Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 118

Chen Tongbai Accompanied Him from Zhejiang - Enthusiastic Reception at the Fish Market

(Right) Dr. Hai Lai (Left) Director Chen

Dr. A. W. Hesse, a famous American fisheries expert, former Director of the Philippine Fisheries Bureau, and current Professor of Ichthyology at Stanford University, came to China on the 15th of last month to investigate China's fisheries. He visited Zhejiang to investigate the aquatic products industry. Yesterday, accompanied by Chen Tongbai, Director of the Zhejiang Fisheries Experiment Farm in Dinghai, he came to Shanghai and, together with Hou Chaohai, Chief of the First Section of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department of the Ministry of Industry, visited Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, in the morning and visited Hujiang University. In the afternoon, he visited the Ministry of Industry and the Shanghai Fish Market. Dr. Hai Lai and Mr. Hou and Mr. Chen went to Dinghai Island at 3:30 PM to arrive at the fish market. They were enthusiastically received by Wang Xiaolai, General Manager of the fish market, Tang Chengzong, Executive Director, Zhu Kaiguan and Sun Gucheng, Deputy Managers, and Zhang Lawei, Section Chief, and they were led to visit the market building and the cold storage. Tea and refreshments were served before leaving at 4:30 PM. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau of this city, hosted a banquet at the Grand East Restaurant at 7:00 PM last night to welcome Mr. Hou Chaohai. Mr. Hou Chaohai also hosted a banquet to welcome him today. Tomorrow noon, all directors and supervisors of the fish market will host a grand banquet at the International Hotel. The fish market directors and supervisors will all be present. It is said that Mr. Hai Lai plans to stay in China for a while and then return to the United States. (Note: Dr. Hai Lai is currently Professor of Ichthyology at Stanford University. When he was the former Director of the Philippine Fisheries Bureau, he transplanted Chinese carp to the Philippines, with very good results. Dr. Hai Lai has written many books and his research on Far Eastern fish is very deep. He has collected fish specimens in many places. He has been to the coastal areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang for the first time. When he was in Dinghai County, he and Lin Shuyan, a technician at the Zhejiang Provincial Aquatic Products Experiment Farm, jointly studied the freshwater fish of the Qiantang River and Zhoushan Island, discovering many new species. Dr. Hai Lai plans to leave Shanghai on the 4th of next month for Hong Kong, Guangzhou, the South Seas Islands, and the Pacific Japanese-occupied islands for investigation and research. He may not be able to return to the United States until next spring. It is reported that Dr. Hai Lai is already sixty-eight years old, but his spirit and physical strength are very strong, and his interest in work is also very high, which is his outstanding point.)

After Jiangsu Province Banned Grain Exports, Shanghai Will Also Properly Arrange Measures - Provincial and Municipal Governments Cooperate to Prevent Unscrupulous Merchants from Manipulating 121

Central News Agency reports that this year, most parts of Jiangsu Province have reported bumper harvests, but the prices of various grains are still rising sharply. One reason is that unscrupulous merchants buy and transport them for export, and the other is that foreign merchants buy them in bulk in the interior. As a result, people are restless and grain prices are rising. Therefore, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, for the sake of maintaining the people's food supply, has strictly prohibited the export of grain and has also imposed controls on transportation to other provinces and cities in the country.

Grain Problem in This City

This city relies on Jiangsu Province for its grain supply. It is learned from grain merchants that the current ban on grain exports formulated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government is not a ban on exports out of the province. Therefore, this city can still have grain produced in Jiangsu Province transported to Shanghai. However, the procedures still need to be approved by the government before passports can be issued for transportation. Therefore, this city hopes that the procedures can be quick and simple, because this city is a commercial and industrial area and has a large population, so it needs a large amount of grain supply from various provinces.

Suzhou and Shanghai Consult on Cooperation

This city is a major trading port, and unscrupulous merchants are very active. Therefore, the city government is also studying detailed measures regarding grain exports. Generally, merchants who transport grain for export must first report to the government the destination and the quantity of transportation before signing the passport. At the same time, the customs must also be notified that exports are only allowed with a passport. Now that the Jiangsu Provincial Government has implemented a ban on grain exports, this city, which is connected to Jiangsu Province, should formulate detailed measures as soon as possible to implement them in order to achieve cooperative results.

Measures to Exempt Cooperatives from Stamp Duty 123

Ministry of Finance Replied to the Municipal Government Yesterday - Except for Accounting Books and Registration Certificates, All Others Should be Affixed with Stamps According to Law

The Ministry of Finance replied to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday, explaining the measures to exempt cooperatives from stamp duty. The letter stated that according to the Shanghai Municipal Government's letter No. 484 of October 8, 1936, submitted by the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, the China Economic Credit Insurance Cooperative requested the Ministry to instruct and verify whether stamp duty can be exempted on the cooperative's books and documents, etc. After reviewing the Cooperative Law's Article 6 stipulates that cooperatives may be exempt from income tax and business tax, but stamp duty and other taxes are not included. The Stamp Duty Law's Article 3, Section 6 stipulates that the certificates used by cooperatives are exempt from stamp duty, which is limited to accounting books. There are no clear provisions for exemption on other certificates. However, the registration certificate issued to the cooperative by the competent authority has been approved by the Ministry of Industry, stating that this registration certificate is issued specifically for inspection and suppression. After verification by the Ministry, it should be exempted in accordance with the provisions of the 32nd item of the Stamp Duty Rate Table's tax-exempt category. Except for accounting books and registration certificates, all other certificates used by the China Economic Credit Insurance Limited Liability Cooperative should be affixed with stamps according to law to emphasize tax law. The aforementioned reply is hereby issued for your review and compliance.

Actual Department Suppresses Yarn and Cotton Speculation, Determines Four Corrective Measures for Observance, Commissioner Resolves to Strictly Supervise Implementation 124

Since Monday, the yarn and cotton market has seen significant fluctuations. Reports indicated that the Ministry of Industry had ordered a strict crackdown on speculation. A reporter from the New News Agency visited the Shanghai Exchange Commissioner. According to him, he had indeed received instructions from the Ministry of Industry to suppress speculation and made the original order public as follows. He also notified the Cotton Cloth Exchange to comply. Yesterday's report stated that the Cotton Cloth Exchange had not yet received the order, which may not be true. The Commissioner also stated that he would always strictly supervise implementation in accordance with the Ministry's order and report to the Ministry at any time.

Ministry of Industry Instruction

Ministry of Industry Instruction No. 48969 Shangzi: It was previously reported by the Wuxi County Cotton Textile Industry Association that the Shanghai Cotton Cloth Exchange had excessive speculation and that cotton merchants were manipulating the market, disrupting real prices and affecting yarn factories. The case was ordered to be thoroughly investigated. Now, this case has been referred by the Ministry to the Ministry of Finance and the Cotton Industry Control Committee for consultation. Discussions were held on the exchange's fixed-term trading periods, futures trading amounts, deposit of margins, and appointment of cotton and yarn appraisers. The following corrective measures have been decided separately (measures recorded below). In addition to notifying the Shanghai Chinese Cotton Cloth Exchange to comply with the above, the commissioner shall supervise and report on the market situation after shortening the exchange's trading period and limiting the trading volume, and whether the margins paid by each broker are in accordance with regulations, and urge compliance. This is the order.

Corrective Measures

(1) The exchange shall order both buyers and sellers to pay the principal margin in accordance with the law. The amount shall be paid in accordance with the ratio stipulated in Article 31 of the Exchange Law. The Exchange Commissioner shall strictly supervise this, and violations shall be punished. (2) The exchange's original fixed-term trading period for cotton and yarn of six months shall be shortened to four months. Initially, it will be reduced in two stages, with each stage reduced by one month, as a trial. (3) Restrictions on the amount of futures trading: (1) The amount of futures trading for each broker in each month shall be limited to 5,000 pieces of cotton yarn and 20,000 dan of cotton. (2) If the limit is exceeded, cotton yarn from 5,050 pieces to 10,000 pieces, and cotton from 20,100 dan to 30,000 dan, in addition to the principal margin, cotton should be charged 10% of the registered price per piece or dan, and cotton yarn should be charged 5%. In addition, a special margin should be charged according to the amount of the principal margin paid, and it cannot be used as a substitute. (3) If the trading volume exceeds 10,000 pieces of cotton yarn, every 5,000 pieces exceeded, and if the trading volume exceeds 30,000 dan of cotton, every 10,000 dan exceeded, the special margin shall be doubled and cannot be used as a substitute. (4) Re-appoint cotton and yarn appraisers: (1) Cotton appraisers should be hired from personnel who have no relationship with the cotton and yarn industries and who can study cotton grading. (2) Cotton yarn appraisers should be hired from personnel who have no relationship with the cotton and yarn industries and who hold a textile technician registration certificate from the Ministry of Industry.

Grain Association Held Emergency Meeting Yesterday 126

Dagong News reports that the Zhejiang Provincial Government recently issued an order from the Department of Civil Affairs to the governments of various counties, strictly prohibiting the export of rice and grain from Zhejiang Province, because the export of rice and grain within the province affects the people's food supply. Therefore, rice transport ships from various gangs have been detained in the Jiaxing and Pinghu areas in recent days, and rice merchants and boatmen have also been arrested. At the same time, the Jiangsu Provincial Government decided at the routine meeting on the 27th to formulate ten provisional measures to strictly prohibit the export of grain, and promulgated them for implementation. The Grain and Oil Cake Industry Association of this city believes that the authorities of the two provinces prohibiting the export of rice affects the people's food supply and has repeatedly received reports from colleagues and rice merchants in various places requesting assistance. Therefore, at 3 pm yesterday, a temporary emergency meeting was convened at the New Kaihe Guild Hall to discuss countermeasures. Chairman Gu Xinyi first had each member report on the situation of rice ships being detained in Zhejiang Province and the strict prohibition of exports in Jiangsu Province, and then began to discuss. The following three measures were decided: (1) Appoint Gu Xinyi, Zhu Zixiang, and Chen Ziyi as three representatives to present a petition to Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government at 2 pm on the 29th (today), requesting that the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces immediately revoke the ban and release the rice ships and merchants. (2) Petition the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward a petition to the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, asking them to consider the people's food supply and revoke the ban. (3) Recommend Gu Xinyi to represent the association to petition the Executive Yuan in Beijing. The meeting adjourned after the discussion. It is reported that Gu will take advantage of the opportunity to present a plane to Beijing to celebrate the birthday and will bring the petition to Beijing on the 31st (tomorrow) to petition the Executive Yuan, requesting that an order be issued to the authorities of all provinces to regulate the national food supply without relying on provincial or municipal administrations.

Party and National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau to Be Closed, Central Government Decides 127

Nanjing, Central News Agency, 28th: The Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior Affairs believe that the Shanghai Party and National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau is not operating well. The Central Government has decided to close it down and has instructed the bureau to comply.

A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically inquired about the truth from Mr. Zhang Rongchu, the person in charge of the bureau. According to him, the bureau received instructions from the Central Propaganda Department and the Ministry of Interior Affairs to close down before the Double Tenth Festival. On the one hand, it immediately stopped manufacturing, and on the other hand, it requested instructions on how to dispose of the inventory and purchased equipment. The bureau currently has an inventory of flags worth 70,000 to 80,000 yuan and equipment worth more than 80,000 yuan. The Party and National Flags that have been manufactured and sold in the past have all been printed in accordance with the methods prescribed by the Central Government. Although the bureau has been ordered to close down, it will continue to sell legitimate Party and National Flags throughout the country. The rest of the equipment and all follow-up matters are still awaiting processing by the Central Government. The Central Government is still promoting the standardization of Party and National Flags.
