Death (Part II) 217

— Liao Chuxiu

Emperor Qin Shi Huang and Emperor Wu of Han were the most famous seekers of immortality. Having the enjoyment of the world, they were naturally unwilling to give up this pleasure and die. Even the supposedly free-spirited scholars and officials of the Wei and Jin dynasties diligently took elixirs. This shows that even those who were "free-spirited" were not careless about life and death. "Death is the only thing difficult since ancient times"?

Once dead, of course, everything is over, and one will no longer feel lonely. Their loneliness about death is felt when they are alive, seeing others die. *Shi Shuo Xin Yu* records:

"When Wang Jun was appointed as Shangshu Ling, he wore his official robes, rode in a light chariot, and passed by the old site of Huang Gong's wine shop. He turned to the guest in the back carriage and said: 'I used to drink here with Ji Shuye and Ruan Sizong, and even participated in the Bamboo Grove gatherings. Since Ji's early death and Ruan's passing, I have been constrained by the times. Although I see this place so close today, it feels as distant as mountains and rivers'!"

"Prince Ziyou and Prince Zijing were both seriously ill, but Zijing died first. Ziyou asked the attendants around him, 'Why haven't I heard any news? He must have passed away.' He didn't show any grief while saying this. Then, he asked for a sedan chair to go to the funeral. He didn't cry at all. Zijing had always loved playing the zither, so he went straight in, sat on the bier, and took Zijing's green zither. The strings were out of tune, so he threw it on the ground and said: 'Zijing, Zijing, both the man and the zither are gone.' Then, he grieved so much that he fainted for a long time. He also died more than a month later."

"A coffin to cover the body, everything is over," this naturally evokes the feeling of a transient life. "How great is death! The virtuous rest, and the petty cease!" In fact, what virtuous and petty people, what heroes and outstanding figures, death truly ends everything. This threat that has existed since life began has made humanity deeply fearful of death. *Shi Shuo Xin Yu* further records:

"Ren Yuchang once passed under a coffin shop, shedding tears of sorrow. Prime Minister Wang said: 'This is a sentimental fool.'" In fact, Prime Minister Wang's words were incorrect. The main reason why Ren Yuchang shed tears was because he felt that his own future would be the same. Therefore, later generations' unwillingness to write about death, and even their avoidance of the word "death," is the extreme expression of this fear of death.

Chekhov, a Russian writer, has a play called "The Life of Man." It is a symbolic play. He uses a gray person holding a candle to symbolize nature. When he first lights the candle, he says: "A person is born." When the candle is halfway burned, he describes various aspects of his life. Finally, when the candle goes out, he says: "This person has died." This gray play powerfully demonstrates the impermanence of life. At the same time, it concretely expresses the concept of death like a candle being extinguished. When we read this play, our hearts can't help but feel heavy.

In addition, I would like to mention a short story called "The Red Laugh." There, the author writes about "death" as "a red laugh, a completely red, toothless laugh." This really scares people.

In Chinese literature, the most relevant work about death is "The Song of Dew on Leeks," but the main idea of this piece is simply that "life is as short as morning dew." Since then, we have seen too many works about this idea. *The Peony Pavilion*: "Such beautiful sights, like water flowing through the years."

Page 18

These two lines have intoxicated many souls. But if readers think carefully, what is the sorrow contained in these two lines, besides the fact that time flows like water, getting closer to death day by day? Although it is said that "beauties have always been like famous generals, not allowed to show white hair in the world," how many white-haired old women were once beautiful beauties? We have not seen anyone commit suicide to maintain their beauty and youth.

Since they are unwilling to be lonely, and they cannot avoid death, they create the idea of consciousness after death and "ghosts" to comfort themselves. Among our acquaintances, we often see elderly people who firmly believe in ghosts and gods. In their youth, they did not believe in them much. The reason is that they know the time of their departure is near. How else can they create a concept to comfort themselves?

Besides believing that there is no consciousness after death, there is also "striving to leave a name behind." This is certainly also an expression of being unwilling to be lonely. However, it is even more "helpless."

"I do not see the ancients before me, nor the followers after me. Thinking of the vastness of heaven and earth, I shed tears in sorrow." In Chen Ziang's poem, we smell the loneliness of death.

Of course, there are also people who are more optimistic about "death." *She Bi Lu* says:

"Duke Pei Jin had a magnanimous nature and did not like to take medicine. He often said to people, 'I eat chicken, pork, fish, and garlic whenever I come across them; when the time comes for birth, old age, sickness, and death, I go.'"

At the same time, Liu Ling carried wine and a shovel, saying, "Bury me when I die." This truly uninhibited spirit not only strongly corrected the then-fashionable practice of "taking elixirs" but also ridiculed many false transcendentalists.

As for modern people, Lu Xun's "Death," published before his death, is also a resolute article about death. Finally, let me copy two idioms as the conclusion: "The dead are gone, how can the living bear it?" This is the reason why I wrote this piece! Jiang Wentong and Li Bai's fu poems are not all about "a soul dying and drinking hatred for thousands of years"?

Le Peiyuan 218

— Especially

—— Come to the Land God Temple on the 23rd of this month, I will be waiting for you in the temple.

A classmate who had been sick for a long time, his environment forced him onto the path of weak decline. A large family, with its exquisite enjoyment, in an ancient city deeply ambushed by opposing forces, does not allow the so-called "young master" to act wantonly. Surrounding him, besides the sounds of mahjong and the aroma of wine, trying to sneak out to a park or a quieter place to get some fresh air is simply out of the question. "Family rules" do not give him such leisure.

As a result, the lung disease is gradually spreading. Food and courses are all out of the question for him. After that, he should still thank the disease for its gift, using the excuse of "seeing a doctor" to come out and thoroughly enjoy the environment outside the "family."

Needless to say, this time he asked me to go to the Land God Temple, using the same method. The purpose is not difficult to imagine. At the end of the letter, he was still afraid of getting the location wrong, specifically pointing out that it was the one near Zhangyi Gate.

I had no way to refuse this request. Counting the days, there were still two days left!

Temple fairs are not uncommon in the ancient city. They are held in rotation every month. The established customs of the Land God Temple on the third day (note) and the Longfu Temple on the tenth are lightly imprinted on the minds of those who are old at running around. It is a bit like a prototype of a "market," but it is much more complete in scale. All kinds of goods extend from the entire temple to half a street. People squeeze, letting the sounds become one. Selection, competition, shouting, scolding... It is so common that it no longer attracts people's attention.

With a happy mood, I arrived at the temple at the appointed time. However, without a relatively fixed location and with so many people, how can I find this small old man afflicted with lung disease? I walked around the connected cloth tents. After walking around, I thought that perhaps he was in the big open space behind the temple, attracted by the lovely flowers and plants. Did that place make him feel an unparalleled interest?

There were also quite a few people here, but where was there any sign of him? Changing to a mood of disappointment, I walked through a path behind me. At the street corner, a sign with "Le Peiyuan" was hung. This alley was strangely unfamiliar. Judging from the terrain, passing through it would definitely lead to the main street.

It was simply another environment. Although it was only separated from the temple by a wall, it was like two different worlds.

The clothes depicted their living conditions. The early autumn wind was blowing. Short clothes, no socks, open chests, it can be said that there was everything. In the two teahouses at the street corner, some people were even sitting with their feet up high, digging out dirt from their feet. The entire winding alley was full of noisy scenes (to be continued).

Movie

Prelude to "Crossroads" 225

This is a play that depicts the situation of graduating and then being unemployed. It is an epitome of the lives of the vast number of Chinese youth. A way out, a way out, where can the youth find a way out in this society? Solving the depression of young people is the theme of this play.

The playwright is Shen Xibao, who has directed "Nostalgia," "Fourteen Hours in Shanghai," and "Boatman's Daughter."

"Crossroads" sketches four intellectual youths living in Shanghai. They are all very kind, but they cannot find a bite to eat in this huge society, even though they have graduated from university. The author has great sympathy for them, but this is not a simple sympathy, but a powerful indication.

The four young people here are: the decadent one, who ends up committing suicide; the active one, who lost his home when he returned from the northeast, and ended up returning to his hometown; and there are two who are both capable and optimistic. They had found jobs, but still lost them. The author here indicates that unemployment is not due to people's lack of effort, but to the entire social problem.

The four roles are played by Zhao Dan, Lü Ban, Yi Ming, and Liu Shangwen, and the female roles are played by Yin and Bai Yang.
